      "authorSolution": "\u003cp\u003eDescribe \u003ca rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003ePicard Iteration\u003c/a\u003e. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eTheorem- Let \\( f(x,t)\\, \\) be continuous for \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |t-t_{0}|\\leq \\alpha ,|x-x_{0}|\\leq \\beta \\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eand satisfy a \u003ca rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003eLipschitz condition\u003c/a\u003e with constant \\( L\\, \\) in this region. Let \\( |f(x,t)|\\leq M\\, \\) there and let \\( \\delta \u003d\\min \\left\\{\\alpha ,\\beta /M\\right\\}\\, \\) . Then the initial value problem \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x(t)\u003dx_{0}+\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}f(x(s),s)ds\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003ehas a unique solution for \\( |t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta \\, \\) . \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eProof- The uniqueness of the solution has already been established in \u003ca rel\u003d\"nofollow\"\u003eODE0.3\u003c/a\u003e. The existence of the solution is proved in three steps. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(i) Define the following sequence of iterates: \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x^{0}(t)\u003dx_{0}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( x^{1}(t)\u003dx_{0}+\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}f(x^{0}(s),s)ds\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e... \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( x^{{N+1}}(t)\u003dx_{0}+\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}f(x^{N}(s),s)ds\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr\u003e The first approximation \\( x^{0}\\, \\) is made by neglecting the integral. The next \\( x^{1}\\, \\) is made by using \\( x^{0}\\, \\) in the intgrand as a correction term. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIn order for the iterates to be defined, it is required to prove that each iterate stays within its domain of definition of \\( f(x,t)\\, \\) . It will be shown that the iterates are defined for \\( |t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta \\, \\) and satisfy the inequalities \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x^{{N+1}}(t)-x_{0}|\\leq \\beta ({\\mathrm {for}}|t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta )\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eThe first step of induction is easy: \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x^{{0}}(t)-x_{0}|\u003d0\\leq \\beta ({\\mathrm {for}}|t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta )\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eThe induction hypothesis is to assume that \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x^{r}(t)-x_{0}|\\leq \\left|\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}|f(x^{N}(s),s)|ds\\right|\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\leq M|t-t_{0}|\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\leq \\beta ({\\mathrm {for}}|t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta )\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eThe completes the induction. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(ii) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNext it is shown that the sequence of iterates is uniformly and absolutely convergent. From the general term of the iteration it is clear that \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x^{{N+1}}(t)-x^{N}(t)\u003d\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}\\left\\{f(x^{N}(s),s)-f(x^{{N-1}}(s),s)\\right\\}ds\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eTake the norm of both sides and use the Lipschitz condition. \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x^{{N+1}}(t)-x^{N}(t)|\\leq L{\\Bigg |}\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}{\\Big |}x^{N}(s)-x^{{N-1}}Big|ds{\\Bigg |}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eThis produces a sequence of inequalities. \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFrom part (i), \\( |x^{1}(t)-x^{0}(t)|\\leq M|t-t_{0}|\\, \\) . \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe induction hypothesis is \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x^{r}(t)-x^{{r-1}}(t)|\\leq ML^{{r-1}}{\\frac {|t-t_{0}|^{r}}{r!}}(r\u003d1,...,N)\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eNow it follows that \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x^{{N+1}}(t)-x^{N}(t)|\\leq {\\frac {ML^{N}}{N!}}{\\Bigg |}\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}|s-t_{0}|^{N}ds{\\Bigg |}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \u003dML^{N}{\\frac {|t-t_{0}|^{{N+1}}}{(N+1)!}}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eNow \\( x^{N}(t)\\, \\) can be written as the partial sum \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x^{0}(t)+\\sum _{{r\u003d1}}^{N}\\left\\{x^{r}(t)-x^{{r-1}}(t)\\right\\}\u003dx^{N}(t)\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eBut the series on the left is domainated term-by-term by the series \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x_{0}+\\sum _{{r\u003d1}}^{N}ML^{{r-1}}{\\frac {|t-t_{0}|^{r}}{r!}}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eAs \\( m\\to \\infty \\, \\) , this series is uniformly and asymptotically convergent to \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x_{0}+{\\frac {M}{L}}\\left[\\exp\\{L|t-t_{0}|\\}-1\\right]\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eSo by the comparison test, \\( x^{N}(t)\\, \\) comverges uniformly for \\( |t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta \\, \\) to a limit function \\( x(t)\\, \\) . \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(iii) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAgain from the general term of the iteration, it can be seen that each iterate is a continuous function of \\( t\\, \\) for \\( |t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta \\, \\) . Hence, since \\( x^{N}(t)\\, \\) converges uniformly to \\( x(t)\\, \\) , it follows that \\( x(t)\\, \\) is a continuous function of \\( t\\, \\) for \\( |t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta \\, \\) . \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eIt follows from \\( |x^{{N+1}}(t)-x_{0}|\\leq \\beta ({\\mathrm {for}}|t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta )\\, \\) that as \\( N\\to \\infty \\, \\) , \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( |x(t)-x_{0}|\\leq \\beta ({\\mathrm {for}}|t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta )\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eIt remains to show that \\( x(t)\\, \\) satisfies the IVP \\( x(t)\u003dx_{0}+\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}f(x(s),s)ds\\, \\) . \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eLet \\( N\\to \\infty \\, \\) in the general iteration term. \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( x^{{N+1}}(t)\\to x(t)\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eand \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}f(x^{N}(s),s)ds\\to \\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}f(x(s),s)ds\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eFinally using the Lipschitz condition, \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003e \\( {\\Bigg |}\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}\\left\\{f(x(s),s)-f(x^{N}(s),s)\\right\\}ds{\\Bigg |}\\leq {\\Bigg |}\\int _{{t_{0}}}^{t}L|x(s)-x^{N}(s)|ds{\\Bigg |}\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\leq L\\delta \\max _{{|t-t_{0}|\\leq \\delta }}|x(t)-x^{N}(t)|\\, \\) \u003c/p\u003e  \n\u003cp\u003eand the right hand side tends to zero as \\( N\\to \\infty \\, \\) . \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e",

In order to do this we will substitute k for the value of n:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\underbrace {{\\sum _{{n\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}2\\left(n+r\\right)\\left(n+r-1\\right)C_{{n}}x^{{n+r}}}}_{{k\u003dn}}-\\underbrace {{\\sum _{{n\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}\\left(n+r\\right)C_{{n}}x^{{n+r}}}}_{{k\u003dn}}+\\underbrace {{\\sum _{{n\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}C_{{n}}x^{{n+r+2}}}}_{{k\u003dn+2}}+\\underbrace {{\\sum _{{n\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}C_{{n}}x^{{n+r}}}}_{{k\u003dn}}\u003d0 \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhich yields:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\sum _{{k\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}2\\left(k+r\\right)\\left(k+r-1\\right)C_{{k}}x^{{k+r}}-\\sum _{{k\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}\\left(k+r\\right)C_{{k}}x^{{k+r}}+\\sum _{{{\\color {red}k\u003d2}}}^{{\\infty }}C_{{{\\color {red}k-2}}}x^{{{\\color {red}k+r}}}+\\sum _{{k\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}C_{{k}}x^{{k+r}}\u003d0 \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eNotice that in the third term, the index of summation, the index for the constant, and exponent of \\( x \\) all changed. Now, in order to add together the sums we need to have the indexes for each sum match. To do this we list the terms for each sum at \\( k\u003d0,1,... \\) until each index is the same. In this example we need to have the \\( k\u003d0 \\) indexes match the \\( k\u003d2 \\) index so we list the terms at \\( k\u003d0 \\) and \\( k\u003d1 \\) . In order to reduce the amount of work required we will add together the sums where \\( k\u003d0 \\) and then factor out the \\( C_{k} \\) term. At this point we can also factor out the \\( x^{r} \\) term.\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\left[\\sum _{{k\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}\\left[2\\left(k+r\\right)\\left(k+r-1\\right)x^{{k}}-\\left(k+r\\right)x^{{k}}+x^{{k}}\\right]C_{{k}}+\\sum _{{k\u003d2}}^{{\\infty }}C_{{k-2}}x^{{k}}\\right]x^{{r}}\u003d0 \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eFrom the sum:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\sum _{{k\u003d0}}^{{\\infty }}\\left[2\\left(k+r\\right)\\left(k+r-1\\right)x^{{k}}-\\left(k+r\\right)x^{{k}}+x^{{k}}\\right]C_{{k}} \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eThe first two terms are:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\left[2\\left(0+r\\right)(0+r-1)x^{{0}}-(0+r)x^{{0}}+x^{{0}}\\right]C_{{0}}\u003d\\left(2r^{{2}}-3r+1\\right)C_{{0}} \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eand\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\left[2\\left(1+r\\right)\\left(1+r-1\\right)x^{{1}}-(1+r)x^{{1}}+x^{{1}}\\right]C_{{1}}\u003d\\left(2r^{{2}}+r\\right)C_{{1}}x \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWhich finally gives us:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\displaystyle x^{{r}}\\cdot \\left[\\left(2r^{{2}}-3r+1\\right)C_{{0}}+\\left(2r^{{2}}+r\\right)C_{{1}}x+\\sum _{{k\u003d2}}^{{\\infty }}\\left[2\\left(k+r\\right)\\left(k+r-1\\right)x^{{k}}-\\left(k+r\\right)x^{{k}}+x^{{k}}\\right]C_{{k}}+C_{{k-2}}x^{{k}}\\right]\u003d0 \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e \n\u003cspan\u003eSolving\u003c/span\u003e \n\u003cp\u003eNow we are ready to solve the equation. We start by equating the terms on the left hand side with the terms on the right hand side (which are all equal to zero). Which gives us the following implications:\u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(1) \\( \\displaystyle \\left(2r^{{2}}-3r+1\\right)C_{{0}}\u003d0\\rightarrow \\left(2r-1\\right)\\left(r-1\\right)C_{0}\u003d0 \\) hence \\( \\displaystyle r\u003d1 \\) and \\( \\displaystyle r\u003d{\\frac {1}{2}} \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(2) \\( \\displaystyle \\left(2r^{{2}}+r\\right)C_{{1}}x\u003d0 \\) hence \\( \\displaystyle C_{1}\u003d0 \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(3) \\( \\displaystyle \\left[2\\left(k+r\\right)\\left(k+r-1\\right)x^{{k}}-\\left(k+r\\right)x^{{k}}+x^{{k}}\\right]C_{{k}}+C_{{k-2}}x^{{k}}\u003d0\\;,\\;k\u003d2,3,4,\\ldots \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e \\( \\;\\Rightarrow C_{{k}}\u003d{\\frac {-C_{{k-2}}}{2\\left(k+r\\right)(k+r-1)-\\left(k+r\\right)+1}}\\;,\\;k\u003d2,3,4,\\ldots \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eWe can now substitute the values for \\( r \\) that satisfy (1) into (3) to yield two different recurrence relations: \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e(4) \\( \\displaystyle r\u003d{\\frac {1}{2}}\\;,\\;C_{{k}}\u003d{\\frac {-C_{{k-2}}}{2\\left(k+{\\frac {1}{2}}\\right)(k+{\\frac {1}{2}}-1)-\\left(k+{\\frac {1}{2}}\\right)+1}}\\;,\\;k\u003d2,3,4,\\ldots \\) \u003cbr\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\Rightarrow \\;C_{{k}}\u003d{\\frac {-C_{{k-2}}}{k\\left(2k-1\\right)}} \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003cbr\u003e \\( \\displaystyle \\Rightarrow \\;C_{{k}}\u003d{\\frac {-C_{{k-2}}}{k\\left(2k+1\\right)}} \\) \u003cbr\u003e\u003cbr\u003e \u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003eAnd then using our values for
